text:
I made this as written, and we enjoyed it. However, if I were to make it again, I would use a hot tangy English mustard (we could barely taste the Dijon), decrease the amount of honey (too sweet for my taste), and use more pecans and less breadrcrumbs (making it more crunchy and flavorsome). The '10 minute per inch of thickness' baking suggestion was absolutely spot-on. Thank you, Christine!

text:
I've been making this recipe since 2002. It's my daughter's favorite meal. I serve it to guests as well as just the family, and it always gets rave reviews. Be sure to use fresh parsley instead of dried - there's a definite difference in flavor. I always use a 2 pound center cut piece of salmon and prepare it early. After putting the topping on the fish, I refrigerate it. I also prepare twice baked potatoes ahead of time and refrigerate those along with asparagus coated with olive oil and garlic salt. When dinner time rolls around, I bake the salmon and potatoes and grill the asparagus on a grill pan - dinner in 20 mins with no fuss! Great for company!

text:
A very elegant salmon! This was wonderful and great tasting. Preparation time was approximate and everything was easy to prepare.  I did tone down on the amount of mustard to 2 T, and butter to 2T, melted. I increased the honey to sweeten up the sauce (personal preference). I seasoned the salmon with a little sea salt and black pepper and then marinated the salmon in the honey, butter, mustard for 6 hours. In a food processor I pulsed fresh italian parsley, 1/4 cup white bread crumbs, and 1 cup organic raw pecans. I pressed the crumb mixture into the salmon before baking at 400 degrees. It took a little longer in baking time because I had thicker cuts of salmon. The results were absolutely amazing! The salmon was light, flaky, sweet and flavorful. I could taste a subtle hint of the dijon mustard. The pecans added a nice texture to the coating of salmon. I served this over a bed of, "Quick and Easy Sautee Spinach," and "Mushroom Rice," all from this website. I will put this in my recipe box and make this again!

text:
It's been a while since I've been amazed by a recipe, but I was truly impressed by this one!  I did not change a thing.  The cooking time is perfect - no over cooked fish here.  I crumbled a slice of whole wheat for the fresh bread crumbs.  I served the fish on a bed of baby spinach sauteed with evoo, garlic, fresh black pepper, and really good quality coarse sea salt.  I also made the Basic Beurre Blanc (French white wine cream sauce), which tied in all the flavors perfectly.  I thought this dish would be a culinary stretch for my hubby, but he finished a huge piece despite not being too hungry.  I wish I could give this 10 stars for being so simple with ingredients and quick with the prep & cooking time.  Fish, spinach, and sauce were on the table in 30 minutes.

The only thing I did differently about this recipe is I used 4tsp of agave nectar (WAY lower glycemic index than honey) instead of 5tsp, because so many people had warned about its being too sweet.  It was a little bit sweet, but I thought the sharpness of the mustard balanced it well.  Also I would highly recommend serving this dish with wild rice - the nutty, heavy flavor of the rice complemented the crisp, sweet topping so, so well.

When the salmon was ready to put in the oven, we had a slight delay and it sat out at room temp. for about 20 minutes with the topping on it. text:
Quite flavorful. I'm going to rate it 5 stars for flavor, but when I make it again, I think it needs minor changes to be considered out of this world. First of all, for 6 pieces of salmon, the mustard/honey mixture should be doubled to easily coat all of the fish. Don't mess with the proportions because the sweet/sour flavor was perfect. FYI, I used the course ground dijon which I think made it extra flavorful. Secondly, the breadcrumbs were a little overwhelming, so I would recommend decreasing maybe by half. In fact I had trouble sprinkling the pecan breadcrumb mixture because the breadcrumbs would clump together. I think it may be easier to coat in breadcrumbs first, and then sprinkle the parsley and nuts on top. I will definitely make this again...oh, and my 4yr old son even gobbled it up!

text:
Great base recipe that you add your own touches to.  I bought a whole fillet with skin on (about 1 1/4 lbs) and sliced it into 8 portions.  Sprinkled fish with salt, pepper, and smoked paprika.  I didn't measure the butter, honey, and mustard mixture - just did it to taste.  Put it on the fish and let it "marinate" in the fridge for a couple of hours.  Toasted the pecans then chopped them in the food processor.  Left out the breadcrumbs and pressed the pecans into the mustard mixture.  Cooking time was perfect.  Absolutely amazing!

text:
Hi Chris,
This recipe was exceptional, and exceptionally easy too!  I used 8 oz. center cut salmon filets, brushed them with the butter mix, and then coated with the crumbs.  I did this early in the day, and just popped it into the oven at dinner.  I baked it using a "slow roast" technique.  Twenty five minutes at 250 degrees.  One other tweaking---instead of 1/2 cup fresh bread crumbs, I used 1/2 cup of dried plain bread crumbs.  I processed the breadcrumbs with the pecans, until a moist meal consistency. Four happy diners last night!
Much thanks,
Jeff

text:
I made this dish for thanksgiving as an entree for my vegetarians.  It was very easy to make and to prep.  I rinsed the fish and laid them out on a cookie sheet and salt and pepper them about two hours before cooking them which helped a lot with timing all the elements of the meal. I personally don't eat fish but I make a lot of it when entertaining.  From what I was told it was delicious.  The topping made it a bit difficult to determine if the fish was done.  It also didn't look as appealing as the picture from the recipe because I used all of the topping that I made per the recipe.  If I make this again I would make less topping and I would chop the pecans and bread more coarsely strictly for presentation.  I gave it 4 stars based on taste per my guests and how quick and easy this was to make.

text:
I made this using halibut instead of salmon.  I also used panko rather than fresh breadcrumbs.  As another reviewer suggested I refrigerated the mustard mixture, which allowed it to thicken.  It then stayed on the fish nicely, instead of running off.  After assembling this I thought it looked a little dry (no doubt due to using panko) so I drizzled it with a little butter just before popping it in the oven.  My halibut was only about a half inch thick but it still took more like 15-20 minutes to bake.  We enjoyed this and I would make it again.  Although if I use panko again, I will toss the topping in melted butter before topping the fish, instead of drizzling it on after.  Good recipe!

Absolutely the BEST fish recipe out there. Even company who don't like fish say it's great. I did make a few changes. text:
I made this for my roommates and even the ones that are avid fish haters loved it.  I added a maple praline to the top of each fillet to bring all the flavors together.  In the future I think I may used crushed pralines instead of pecans.  To make the pralines us pecans, maple syrup, some honey, and maybe a bit of sugar.  Heat in a small sauce pan until it is just barely bubbling, then spoon small bunches onto wax paper and wait to cool.  The maple flavor helped to mix the sweetness of the pecans and the flavor of the salmon.

text:
"Oh my God, my girlfriend can cook!" was my boyfriend's reaction to this dish. This was my first time making salmon so I was a little skeptical about the results. I had just regular mustard, not dijon, and didn't use any nuts. I followed the rest of the recipe, and in addition, I added half a tsp of crushed ginger and garlic, a sprinkle of chili powder, oregano and about half a tsp of chili sauce. After the fish had been in the oven for 10 minutes, I sprinkled the fish with bread crumbs and crushed red pepper flakes. When finished, it looked really impressive and the flavour was just awesome and spicy, but also a little sweet from the honey! Very moist, but not at all soggy. Would definitely make this again!

If you're looking for an impressive dish to serve company (or to spoil your family any time), this is it. text:
Perfect recipe! Made it for the whole family and they loved it. 

The only adjustments I would make is cutting the bread/pecan recipe by half ATLEAST. Probably a 1/3 of the amount would be fine. I had lots of leftover mix. Also I used honey mustard instead of dijon mustard because that's what I had on hand.

As for baking, 10 mintures per inch of salmon is a good starter. I baked it for about 15 minutes and it was fine. 

I also made my own sauce to go with the dish that gave the sweet salmon a tinge of sourness. A simple mixture of heavy whipping cream, salt, lemon juice, fresh parsley, and a little bit of butter.

This will definitely be my go to salmon recipe from now on!

text:
I made this recipe as directed but I doubled the topping ingredients both dry and wet because we wanted a lot of topping to fish ratio.    I followed the directions and brushed the sauce on the fillets and topped them with the breadcrumbs (I used panko)  and pecan mixture.   When I was finished I dripped the remaining sauce on top of the dry ingredients too.    10 minutes per a inch of thickness was perfect.    My husband and I both absolutely loved this.  None of the ingredients overwhelm or call attention to themselves.   The flavors of the topping and the fish come together in this wonderful cacophony that is indescribably wonderful.   It is was one of those dishes where you go, "This is AMAZING what is in it???"  And then go back to the restaurant and order it over and over trying to figure it out.   I covered my pan in regular foil and then put a piece of non stick foil at the top (which is more expensive) so nothing stuck and there was no clean up either.   This is going to be permanently added to the dinner rotation.

text:
I live in Seattle, so I eat a lot of salmon, and every restaurant in town has at least one salmon recipe on the menu.  I am so picky about my salmon that I won't eat it anywhere outside the pacific coastline where it is fresh and restaurants don't over-cook it (seriously landlocked cities, try taking the fish out a little earlier, it shouldn't be chewy!!!) I wanted to try a new recipe since we have salmon at least once a week, and I am getting bored of the same old recipes.  This one was fantastic! I don't really like mustard, so I cut it back to 2 T, and we didn't have dijon, so I used a spicy sweet mustard instead.  I also took a reviewer's instruction and increased the ratio of pecans to breadcrumbs (changed pecans to 2/3 cup and breadcrumbs to 1/3 cup) otherwise we cooked it exactly as written.  This is definitely going in the regular rotation.  Thanks!

text:
This is the best salmon recipe on earth, as far as I'm concerned!  I have just a couple of tips:  Tip #1:  Don't brush the fillets.  Put the glaze in a shallow bowl and dip each fillet in it quickly before placing it on your cooking pan. Tip #2:  Use a Silpat (a silicone pad that is made for cooking pans so bottoms of foods don't get overcooked or burnt onto your nice cookware)--the clean up is so much easier. Tip #3:  If you don't have a food processor, the crust might be frustrating to create.

text:
I had 4 frozen salmon fillets and was not quite sure what to do with it until I found this recipe.  I prepared the marinade with a few additions:  added 1/2 tsp minced garlic, 2 tbs mayonaise, and I used honey mustard dressing since I didn't have any dijon on hand.  I covered the fillets in the marinade while they were still frozen and covered the cookie sheet with wax paper and allowed the fillets to thaw and marinate over night.  The next day, I scraped off the marinade and added more honey, mayo, butter and dressing, and also blended in 1/2 cup seasoned bread crumbs and parsley. This was then used to cover the fillets.  I baked at 400 for 12 mins (based on the rec of 10 min per inch of thickness) and then turned the broiler on high for approx 2 minutes.  The fillets were flakey and juicy and everyone loved it.

I am going to try one more time because of the number of good reviews this got, but I will make a "crumb topping" with the melted butter so it will crisp up.

text:
This is a very good salmon recipe.  It was a tad too sweet when I made it the first time, so I used about half the amount of honey called for when I made it subsequently, This turned out to be perfect for my taste .  I also agree with another reviewer that it helps to leave the butter (or I used non-hydrogenated tub margarine) semi-solid. Don't melt it too much, if at all.  It stays on the salmon better and seems to make for a better end product (more moist and the topping sticks better).  I will make again and again.  Thanks!

text:
This was very good! I still couldn't get my 10-year-old to eat salmon, but I enjoyed it. While the flavor, texture, and presentation were good, I can't give it 5 stars because I almost felt like I was putting too much other 'stuff' on the salmon, thus detracting from its natural goodness. I may make this again, but if I do, I will decrease the bread crumbs and pecans.

Because I couldn't find 'easy' bread crumbs at the store that didn't contain high-fructose corn syrup and partially hydrogenated fats, I toasted a couple slices of organic "Women's Bread," then threw it in my food processor. It was the perfect addition. I think next time I'll substitute plain yogurt for the butter, too. Then I don't have to worry at all about the healthfulness of this dish. Thanks for the recipe!

text:
This is wonderful.  I used Extra Virgin Olive Oil instead of butter to make it healthier.  I also used Panko bread crumbs so it would be lighter.  I mixed in a little olive oil into the bread crumb mixture to make them stick together a little better.

I used a filet with the skin on and seared the filet, skin side down, in a pan on the stove before I put it in the oven to make the skin crispy, the fish comes off of the skin better when eating it.

text:
Made this last night. Next time I will cut the honey by 1/2. The butter/honey/mustard mix is good, but comes out too sweet and overpowers the Dijon flavoring. Cut the honey in 1/2 for sure. I let the salmon marinate for 20-30 minutes, and also had to bake it at 400 for close to 25 minutes versus the author's  "10 minutes per inch". That simply would have not been cooked thoroughly enough. Also, I used walnuts instead of pecans, and Japanese Panko breadcrumbs - got a great result. I will definitely be making this again, using less honey and baking for 20+ minutes. Served this with sauteed zucchini, red pepper & green pepper (in olive oil, garlic, balsamic and red wine vinegar).

text:
This is a wonderful recipe that I make for company.  To make the coating crunchier, I omit the bread crumbs and just use the chopped pecans (walnuts work too) and parsley.  Ten minutes in the oven wan't long enough the first time I made this. Even though the salmon filllets were not more than an inch thick, they were very large.  Make sure to test the thickest part with a fork before serving.  I serve this with asparagus and whole grain & wild rice.

text:
Wow, this is restaurant quality!  I, too, used a store bought honey mustard and mixed that with the melted butter.  I didn't have any bread crumbs so I just sprinkled the salmon with salt & pepper and then a little dried italian spice mix which contained parsley. Then I sprinkled on the ground pecans and baked for 11 minutes.  At the end of baking I turned on the broiler and let the pecans toast a little more, just about 2 or 3 minutes before removing from the oven.  Watch carefully, though.  This was so yummy even without the bread crumbs, which saved a few calories, too!

Made this last night and thought it was SO delicious. The sweet flavors of the honey mixed with the tangy mustard and nutty pecans. I am not even a big fan of honey or dijon, but the flavors mixed were amazing. My boyfriend isn't a big fish fan, but he ate his up quickly and admitted it was really good. The only change I (accidently) made was that I let the salmon soak in the honey/butter/mustard mixture for about 20 minutes, sort of like a marinade. I don't think it made much difference, but it may have infused more sweetness into the salmon.

text:
I made this for myself for Christmas.  Best Christmas dinner ever!!  I only made minor changes.  I had an entire filet (28 oz) so I cut it in half and only used half the ingredients.  I used French's Honey Dijon instead of regular dijon and honey, since I already had it.  Like other reviewers, I increased the pecans and decreased the breadcrumbs (2/3 and 1/3), but I didn't actually use breadcrumbs.  I used Ritz crackers.  (Saw it in another review.)  I don't have a brush, so I slathered the mustard mixture on with my hands (fun, but messy!) then pressed the crumb mixture onto it.  I also drizzled melted butter on top before baking.  It was FABULOUS!  I can't wait to make the other half!

text:
A very nice change of flavor for salmon! The crunch of the pecan lends an almost meat-like heartiness. I used honey mustard (for lack of dijon), cut down to 2 tsp of honey and 1 Tbsp butter, cut breadcrumbs to 1/3 cup and increased pecans to 2/3 cup. I also covered the salmon in the mustard sauce and then dredged it in the pecan/breadcrumb mixture and baked in foil packets. A quick, delicious dinner! ~UPDATE~ I am giving this a fifth star... I used dijon this time and let the mustard mixture sit in the fridge a bit before spreading it on the fish; the fish then marinated in the fridge for a while before I sprinkled on the pecan mixture. Baked on a sprayed cookie sheet... my family devoured this.

YUMMY!  I used some of the reviews and used 2 T. butter, 2 T. mustard (spicy brown), and the 5 t. honey.  I didn't measure the crumbs but used 2 slices of bread and a couple small handfuls of pecans.  I didn't have fresh parsley so used dried.  I also refrigerated the mustard mix first so it was thick.  Very yummy--will be a staple of my salmon repertoire.

text:
This was very good.  It isn't quite THE recipe to make me toss all others, but it is very much a repeater.  I'd suggest either making sure you're using pre-flavored breadcrumbs or that you get more liberal with your seasonings in the dry mix because it was just a tad bland even after using spicy mustard.  **edit** I originally reviewed this in March of 2008 and only gave it 4 stars. I've changed my mind entirely. This is delicious and has become a staple at out house.  Just don't forget to s&p the fillet before topping. I get a bit more liberal with the spices and we throw these on the grill in tinfoil trays. EVERYTHING tastes better off the grill!  Just triple layer some foil, triple fold the edges and pull them up to make sides.  You can just toss it when you're done...

I cooked this for my parents and they LOVED it! I didn't have any dijon mustard so i just used regular old yellow mustard. And, i reduced butter by half and added a little mayo instead. I accidentally put less honey than supposed to, but the stil fish came out really nice and creamy. I also used store bought italian bread crumbs along with pecans and almonds. The nuts became sweet and carmelized  and were awesome! My mom also insisted i add some onions on the side of the baking dish because she likes veggies. The onions also carmelized with the sauce and came out wonderful. Served with brown rice, with carmelized onions, salmon with pecan/almond on top. It was a wonderful meal and my parents were Very impressed. next time ill make a little more sauce to put on the side for veggies. Oh, and im a college student (not an experienced cook) and this recipe was super easy and fast!

This was very good, everyone thought I was a natural gourmet. I used Grey Poupon (my boyfriend went shopping as I would have bought something cheaper) and cut down to 2.5 TBS but I think the whole 3 would have been fine.  When I first mixed it, I thought the mustard was, too, much and my boyfriend would not like it but it was excellent when it was done. I even used the extra sauce as dip.  My salmon was about 1 and a half inch at its thickest point so I baked for 20 minutes and the topping and sides were done but the middle was not hot all the way through so I covered with foil to not over brown the topping and cooked another 6-8 minutes more.  It was great. I used one and a half slices of Stroehmann King Bread and put it in the food processor.  I will definitely make this again. My boyfriend loves salmon and eats at a number of restaurants and thought this was great.  I served with some wilted spinach and white rice.

I'm sorry but contrary to all the great reviews, I was very disappointed.  First of all, there is way too much mustard - it overpowers the sweetness of the honey.  Secondly, salmon is such an oily fish it really doesn't need so much butter.  I really would have liked to taste the honey and should have followed my instincts in reducing the amount of mustard to a teaspoon or so.  I also had the idea of doing a fresh ginger honey glaze to brighten up the flavors.  Overall, this recipe was nothing special.  I probably won't make it again without altering it so much that it becomes another recipe entirely.

Sorry!!

I live in a landlocked Mid-Western state where beef is king.  I admit that this recipe was my first attempt of preparing fresh fish at home.  This is one area of cooking where I am a true novice, but this recipe turned out fabulous!  My husband and I really enjoyed it. I also crushed the pecans very fine (approximately the same texture as the bread crumbs) because my husband is not a big fan of nuts.  Guess what, he didn't even realize this had nuts in it!  Thank you Chris for making my first attempt at preparing salmon a success.

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
I changed the recipe slightly and it was a great dish!!! I omitted the bread crumbs completely. I waited for the honey mustard mixture to cool before spreading maybe about half of the mixture on the salmon (enough that there was a nice coating without pouring off the fish) and refrigerated it for a 30 minutes. I keep the left over honey mustard mixture and made a cream sauce with it. The pecans stuck perfectly to the salmon when I was ready to put it in the oven. And I baked it as directed. For the cream sauce I added half a cube of vegetable bouillon to a cup of boiling water, then stirred in 3 tbsp of cornstarch and one clove of minced garlic . I put that in a sauce pan on med low, then added 3/4 cup of cream (milk would also work fine) then added the remaining honey mustard mixture. Let that come to a simmer and reduce the heat to low, stirring often. I'd say it would be ready in about 5 mins. Was awesome! Also this is gluten free if that's important to you. Thanks for the recipe!!!

text:
I made this as written and thoroughly enjoyed it. The only thing I forgot to add was the lemon, but it honestly didn't make or break the recipe. This was my first time working with salmon... I mean really working with it. Any other day I would just slap a few spices on it and stick it in the oven for a few minutes. Today however I wanted to get creative, and use the bag of pecans I purchased at work.
The sweetness of the honey works really well with the Salman. Sadly I didn't have normal honey, but a jalapeno honey I bought from the Farmers Market. The spice really added a bit of flavor, so no harm there. Next time I will more than likely mix the dry ingredients into the wet. That was the only problem I had with the cooking process because the dry ingredients didn't bake too well. Otherwise, great recipe. Will definitely make again, once I figure out what to pair it with. This time I wind up using a black rice, but that was a bit on the dull side.

text:
Success! Used walnuts instead of pecans, it's what I had, and for the breadcrumbs used panko. I added some finely chopped fresh tarragon and thyme from my garden instead of the parsley. As written I was sure it would be too sweet for my taste so I decreased the honey by about half and that turned out perfect for me. I couldn't really taste the mustard; either I'll increase the amount next time or opt for a stronger flavored whole grained brand instead of the generic smooth Dijon. Before putting in the oven I spritzed the topping with an olive oil spritzer to make sure the topping browned nicely and it looked beautiful. I'm definitely making this again and keeping this recipe.

text:
After using this recipe for so many years, I thought it was about time I wrote to thank "Chris" who submitted it!  It's been my go-to salmon recipe for such a long time now, and the only changes I made were to make an easy recipe even easier! I use panko crumbs instead of fresh (no crumbling needed)and instead of putting the raw pecans on the salmon before baking, I use the tiny pre-toasted pecan pieces from Trader Joe's (Yes, I am that lazy!) and sprinkle them on before serving along with dried parsely. Like reviewer Santon, I wait until the topping mixture thickens before I slather it on.  Thank you, Chris!

text:
My husband really enjoyed this, but my two sons (who usually do like salmon) wouldn't touch it.  I thought it was good, but not quite as good as some of the other recipes we have used to prepare salmon in the past.  I think the quality of the ingredients makes a big difference, I read some reviews that stated that there was not a lot of flavor, but I used a high quality full strength stone ground mustard and a good local honey and we had no problems with depth of flavor.   put fresh french bread and pecans in the food processor for the breading and it turned out great.  I did use another reviewer's tip on refrigerating with the mustard sauce spread on it for about 20 min before cooking.  thanks for the recipe!

Delicious stuff!  I'm not a fan of measuring, so I don't really know how much of the ingredients I used, but it's easy enough to put together.  Instead of brushing on the honey, dijon, and butter mixture, I dipped the salmon in it then dipped in the pecan and bread crumb mix, like you would do for fried chicken.  That way was a bit messier, but I was able to coat all of the salmon.  Bf and I both loved it, and bf didn't even notice there was dijon mustard in the salmon.  (He hates mustard)  Thank you very much for the recipe!  We'll make again.  :o)

Spectacular Dish.
I used just a little less honey.  I used a white sage raw honey which I buy threw EBay from The Flying bee Ranch.   This honey made such a smooth wonderful sweetness to the salmon.   
I used less bread crumbs & more pecans.  I usually make my own but this time I used Contadina Roasted garlic and savory herb.  It was good and quick.  
I fixed this for my book club and everyone was moaning.  It was a very nice dinner. 
I put the fish on top of a bed of creamy mashed potatoes and served with steamed asparagus, Caesar salad, Rosemary homemade bread and English Trifle.

Delicious! I used dried tarragon because I didn't have any parsley and added soy sauce, fresh lemon juice and fresh minced garlic to the mustard mixture. I brushed some of the mustard mixture onto the fish then mixed the rest with the pecan crumb mixture and spread it on top. Baked for 20 mins (2-inch thick fillet) at 400 degrees. Wonderful flavor. Next time I might marinate the salmon in soy sauce for 30 mins before coating with the toppings. Served this with fresh broccoli and cauliflower and brown rice. Great recipe, thanks for sharing!

text:
I'm giving this four stars because the recipe has some potential.  We made some of the changes suggested such as decreasing the bread crumbs, increasing the pecans, and adding the topping at the last minute.  I found the flavor overall to be bland.  I've had pecan coated trout and salmon in restaurants before and it was better.  I found the topping to be a bit dry.  Next time, I think we'll drizzle more butter over the pecans.  The topping which fell off the salmon and baked on the bottom of the pan with the butter and juices was better than on top of the fish.
